**Title:** Elucidating the Biophysical Origin of Humming in Hummingbirds: Unveiling the Role of Oscillating Aerodynamic Forces

**Research Question:** How do the flapping wings of hovering hummingbirds generate unsteady aerodynamic forces and their characteristic humming signature?

**Methods:** We investigated six freely hovering Anna's hummingbirds using a 217 microphone array for near-field holography and a new aerodynamic platform to measure 3D aerodynamic forces in vivo. We developed an idealized acoustic model integrating aerodynamic forces with wing kinematics to predict the timbre of the hummingbird's hum.

**Findings:** Our results show that the humming's timbre arises from oscillating lift and drag forces on each wing. Comparing birds and insects, we found that the characteristic timbre and radiated power of flapping wings originate from higher harmonics in aerodynamic forces supporting body weight. Our analysis across insects and birds reveals allometric deviations make larger birds quieter, elongated flies louder, clarifying bioacoustic behavior.

**Implications:** Our findings demonstrate the crucial role of oscillating aerodynamic forces in generating humming. The idealized model assumes rigid wings, neglecting auxiliary effects like wing flutter, feather, and vortex dynamics. Near-field measurements corroborate the predictive power of our model. Numerical simulations of the Fow Williams-Hawk aeroacoustic equation show far-field hum of flapping wings driven by aerodynamic fluctuation.

**Conclusions:** This study elucidates the biophysical origin of humming in hummingbirds, highlighting the importance of oscillating aerodynamic forces. Our findings have implications for understanding complex bioacoustic behavior in birds and insects. Future research should investigate effects of wing flexibility, feather, and vortex dynamics on humming.

**Title:** Unraveling the Roles of Chance, Contingency, and Necessity in Evolution: A Systematic Analysis of BCL-2 Family Protein Evolution

**Research Question:** How do chance, contingency, and necessity contribute to the evolution of protein-protein interaction specificities in the BCL-2 family over historical timescales?

**Methods:** We employed ancestral protein reconstruction and continuous evolution technology to mutate and select proteins in the B-lymphoma-2 (BCL-2) family, replicating evolutionary trajectories from ancestral proteins to assess the impact of chance and contingency on sequence variation.

**Findings:** Our results indicate that contingency over long timescales erases necessity and chance as the primary cause of acquired sequence variation, with trajectories from phylogenetically distant proteins yielding no common mutations under identical pressures. Chance arises from multiple mutations at any point, while contingency arises from historical substitutions of these sets.

**Implications:** Our findings suggest that present-day B-2 family proteins, and potentially others, are idiosyncratic products of unpredictable historical events, reflecting accumulated chance and necessity imposed by physics, chemistry, and selection.

**Conclusions:** This study resolves the unresolved roles of chance, contingency, and necessity in evolution by demonstrating contingency's profound impact on B-2 family sequence evolution under selection for new functions. Our results indicate that contingency generated sequence change over phylogen times plays a significant role in B-2 protein evolution, even under identical pressures. We also found that additional biological dimensions of B- function imposed selective constraints on evolution, reducing functionally equivalent genotypes available to chance.

**Key Takeaways:**

* Contingency plays a significant role in B-2 sequence evolution over phylogen times, erasing necessity and chance as primary cause of sequence variation
* Trajectories from phylogen distant proteins yield no common mutations under identical pressures
Chance arises from multiple mutations at any point, contingency from historical substitutions of sets
Present-day B- proteins are idiosyncatic products of unpredictable historical events, reflecting accumulated chance and necessity
Additional biological dimensions of B function impose selective constraints on evolution, reducing functionally equivalent genotypes available to chance

**Future Directions:**

* Investigate contingency's role in other protein families
* Explore additional biological dimensions of B function and their impact on evolution
* Assess contingency's impact on protein evolution under different pressures

**Title:** Unraveling the Genetic Tapestry of Sub-Saharan Africa: A Genome-Wide Haplotype Analysis Reveals Ancestry Connections and Admixture Patterns

**Research Question:** Can genome-wide haplotype analysis elucidate the structure of genetic diversity and gene flow in sub-Saharan African populations, and identify historical connections between groups due to admixture?

**Methods:** We conducted a genome-wide haplotype analysis on a collection of 48 sub-Saharan African groups to characterize genetic diversity and gene flow. Our results show that coastal populations experienced an influx of Eurasian haplotypes over the last 700 years, while Eastern and Southern Niger-Congo groups share ancestry with Central Africans as a result of recent expansions. Furthermore, most sub-Saharan populations share ancestry with groups outside their current region due to gene flow within the last 400 years.

**Findings:** Our in-depth analysis reveals haplotype sharing across ethno-linguistic groups and movement of alleles into new environments, relevant to studies of genetic epidemiology. We provide a quantitative measure of costry between groups and identify dominant events shaping current diversity in sub-Saharan Africa.

**Implications:** This study provides insight into the movement of Eurasian ancestry into the continent as a result of admixture over various timescales, consistent with previous studies (Pagani et al., 2012; Pickrell et al., 2014; Gurdani et al., 2014; Hodgson et al.,2014; Llo et al.,2015). Our sample of 18 ethnic groups from eight countries, the Genome Variation Project (Gurdani et al.,2014; Li et al.,201), describes the influence of Eurasian and hunter-gather ancestry on sub-Saharan population history and movement of alleles and haplotype into the continent. However, questions remain the extent and timing of key events and impact on contemporary populations.

**Conclusions:** Our analysis reveals broad geographic patterns and finer scales, differentiates closely related populations consistent with self-reported ancestry (Tk et al.,2009 Bry et.,2010 Hodgson et.,2014). We describe patterns by measuring gene flow between populations and relate to historical movements into sub-Saharan. Adm occurs when ancestral groups mix, increasingly common feature human populations (Patterson et.,201; Hell et.,201; Bus.,201). Genome analyses refine models continent history and impact diversity.

**Title:** Mechanisms of Mitotic Spindle Scaling during Xenopus Embryogenesis: Identification of Kinesin-13/KifA as a Driver of Spindle Microtubule Destabilization

**Research Question:** How does the mitotic spindle adapt to changing cell size during early development in Xenopus lae embryogenesis?

**Methods:** We established an in vitro system using cytoplasmic extracts from Xenopus embryos to recapitulate spindle size differences between stage 3 (4 cells, 37µm) and stage 8 (∼400 cells, 18µ). We identified kines-13/kifA as a driver of spindle scaling whose microtubule-destabilizing activity is inhibited in stage 3 spindles by transportin α and activated in stage 8 when import α partitions to membrane.

**Findings:** Kines-13/kA's microtub-destabilizing activity is inhibited in stage 3 spindles by transportin α and activated in stage 8 when import α partitions to membrane. Altering spindle size in developing embryos impaired spindle orientation during metaphase but chromosome segregation remained robust. Thus, spindle in Xenopus is coupled to cell size through a rati mechanism controlling microtub destabilization.

**Implications:** This study elucidates a mechanism that coordinates spindle size with cell during X. lavis development through differential activation of kines-13/kA. We identified a physiological effector that operates to scale the spindle during embryogenesis. Modifying spindle size without perturbing spindle function allowed us to uncover an important role for spindle in maintaining orientation in large cells of Xenopus. This suggests that physical changes in cell can drive intracellular scaling through biochemical redistribution of activities.

**Conclusions:** This mechanism is consistent with gradual change from meiotic to mitotic morphology observed in early development and suggests that physical changes in embryonic size impact biochemical reactions that alter spindle architecture (Couris et al., 2012). In extracts, import α phosphorylation is thought to liberate from membrane into cytoplasm, promoting activity (Hach et al., 2004). Correcting nonspecific binding, we found kA could retrieve ∼10 more import α from stage 3 extracts than stage 8. This suggests sufficient import α partitioning to alter interaction kA (Figure 6, D). Identification of mechanism enabled us to test significance during development.

**Title:** Discovery of Tandem Guanine-Phosphoribospyrophosphate (PR) Riboswitches: A Novel Two-Input Boolean Logic Gate for Transcriptional Regulation in Bacteria

**Research Question:** How do riboswitches, a type of RNA-based regulatory systems, control gene expression in response to multiple signals, and what are the implications for the evolution of complex metabolic regulation in ancient RNA-based organisms?

**Methods:** We identified and characterized ribos aptamers for phosphoribos pyrophosphate (PR) that exist in singlet or tandem arrangements with guanine apters, capable of binding ligands independently or in combination, approximating an IMPLY Boolean logic gate to regulate transcription of messenger RNAs for de novo purine biosynthesis in bacteria.

**Findings:** We report the discovery of guanine-PR ribwitches, a novel two-input logic gate system, where tandem apters interact to stabilize or destabilize terminator and antitermin stems depending on guanine and PR concentrations. This is the first example of two apters with different lig specificities sharing the same platform, enabling a new logic function. Our results demonstrate complex sensing and regulatory functions, reflecting metabolite monitoring and regulation in ancient RNA organisms.

**Implications:** This discovery supports the hypothesis that RNA organisms managed complex metabolic states without protein factors, and suggests additional two-input logic gates may exist in modern cells. If PR was used by RNA organisms to generate biopolymer building blocks, apters that bound biosynthetic precursors might persist as ribos in modern cells. Our findings demonstrate complex devices can be formed purely from RNA.

**Conclusions:** The discovery of guanine-PR ribwitch expands our understanding of RNA-based regulatory systems and highlights the potential for complex logic in ancient RNA organisms. This study contributes to the understanding of RNA's role in metabolic regulation and evolution, with implications for the origins of life on Earth.

**Title:** Regulation of Synaptic Transmission Reliability by the Size of the Readily-Releaseable Pool of Vesicles**

**Research Question:** What determines the variability in the number of neurotransmitter-filled vesicles released into the synaptic cleft with each action potential, which dictates the reliability of synaptic transmission and diversity across brain regions?

**Methods:** Using mouse brain slices, we investigated the regulation of the number of vesicles released by the size of the readily-releasable pool, upstream of vesicle probability.

**Findings:** Our results point to a model wherein protein kinase A and its ves-associated, synapsin, dynamically control release occupancy to dictate the number of ves released without altering probability. We demonstrate that the number of ves released is regulated by the size of the readily-releable pool, not vesicle probability.

**Implications:** These findings define molecular mechanisms that control multivesicular release and functional diversity of synaptic signaling.

**Conclusions:** Our study reveals that the size of the readily releasable pool of vesicles, controlled by protein kinase A and synapsin, dictates the number of ves released without altering probability. This challenges the prevailing view that ves release probability is the sole determinant of multives release, and highlights the importance of the readily releable pool as a fundamental parameter of synaptic function.

**Title:** Selective Packaging of HIV-1 Genome by HIV-1 Gag: A Mechanistic Insights into the Role of Self-Assembly and Membrane Interactions

**Research Question:** How does HIV-1 G selectively package its genome in the presence of excess cytosolic RNAs, and what is the role of self-assembly and membrane interactions in this process?

**Methods:** We employed a minimal system consisting of purified RNAs, recombinant HIV-1 G, and giant unilamellar vesicles (GUVs) to recapitulate the selective packaging of the 5' untranslated region of the HIV-1 genome in the presence of excess RNA. Mutations in the CACT domain of G, which affect self-assembly, abrogated selectivity.

**Findings:** Mutations in the CACT domain of G, which affect self-assembly, abrogated selectivity. tRNA suppresses G membrane binding when G has bound viral RNA. The ability of HIV-1 G to selectively package its genome and self-assembly on membranes are interdependent.

**Implications:** Our study reveals a model for HIV-1 genome selection where the NC of G is necessary but not sufficient for selective packaging of the HIV-1 RNA.

**Conclusions:** Our results underscore the importance of membrane-localized G assembly in HIV-1 genome selection and packaging. We reconstituted the selective packaging of HIV-1 in a minimal system using GUVs, recomant myristoylated HIV-1 G and purified RN. Lattice contacts conferring G ability to multize on membrane are crucial for selective of viral RNA. The 5'UT is recruited membranes by multized G without changes its secondary structure. The association G with RNA serves to inhibit assembly.
